< text>
I swore that Santo Market was the best poke, but Aloha Fresh makes me question myself. They are owned by a Hawaiian staff and serve top quality poke. The best part is that they try to stay as traditional as possible while still appealing to people who haven't had real Hawaiian poke.

I find myself going there at least once a week and always get the Poke Lover with Hawaiian Ahi, Spicy Ahi, crab salad, and ocean salad.

This might be the best poke spot outside of Hawaii ü§î</text>

< review>
The only poke place in the bay that brings me back to Hawaii. Good quality fish, excellent flavors. None of the excessive random fillers that other ‚Äúbuild your own poke bowls‚Äù have, and no awkward texture pieces of fish. Just pure delicious poke & hot rice - exactly like Hawaii :) they also sell poke by the pound, other hot Hawaiian foods, and Hawaiian snacks. If we lived closer, we‚Äôd definitely be coming more often! Even still, it‚Äôs worth a 30 min drive whenever I need my Hawaiian poke fix.

To top it off, staff are friendly & portions are huge- I couldn‚Äôt finish my bowl even after going on a hike and only having eaten a granola bar earlier! (Unlike those other poke places that fill the bowl with rice or salad, aloha fresh loads you up on what actually matters- the poke & equally delish sides!)< /review>

Delicious and fresh poke bowls. $15 for a really small size. The portion is so small that I'd never finished a poke without rice and salad remaining on the bottom. The rice and salad are so so so much lesser than others. I only saw a few greens lying in my bowl. Don't know why they give so small amount of rice and veggies when they have such good proteins and sides. Maybe I'll go for somewhere else instead.</text>

<Date>1541049823257<//Date><Review>New poke place in Japantown. A proper one that marinates the fish instead of mixing it in a bowl in front of you like some other fast casual poke concepts. This is Hawaiian style poke.

I had the Spicy Ahi Shoyu and Spicy Salmon. Tasty but pretty mild on the heat scale. I'm not looking to burn my taste buds but I expect a little more zing when I order something spicy. I also missed that they didn't have furikake for the rice.

Kailua pork is also on the menu. I might try that next time.< /Review>< Response>

<Gmap_id>0x808fcd7b622c3c4d:0xa702f01cb9ac0857< /Gmap_id>< Text>
Aloha Fresh (along with Santo Market down the street) has hands down the best poke in the Bay. Unlike all of the Chipotle-style fast casual poke places that have popped up in the last few years, Aloha Fresh actually marinates their fish and uses traditional Hawaiian flavors/ingredients and it makes a huge difference. Spicy shoyu ahi and miso salmon are my go-tos here, but you can't really go wrong with any of the flavors.</Text>

<rating>3</rating><Text>Pros: You can get poke with something like inamona on it ("kukui nut" flavor) and they do give you the option of buying poke by weight instead of having to get one of those awful everything-but-the-kitchen-sink things that mainlanders think are great.

Cons: What's the deal with the loud, obnoxious, raggae music? A grand total of no one listens to this stuff in Hawaii. There's a huge, HUGE, body of work by Hawaiian musicians from the early 20th century on, "Slack Key" guitar, just tons of music that's much nicer to listen to, and actually would be much more proper to play in an ostensibly "Hawaiian" place, and might introduce more mainland people to a genre of music they'd enjoy.

Seriously, all the "Hawaiian" places here on the mainland do this, and it's a huge slight to actual Hawaiian music by actual Hawaiian people.< /Text>< Pictures>

< text>
Ended up going here because in the Lamorinda area you have maybe two options for breakfast around 6am. I decided to give them a shot, and I will not be going back. The food was not appetizing at all. My friend took one bite of his scrambled eggs and ham and put his fork down, and that dude eats just about anything. It was like cafeteria food. I can see how since it's the only game in town that people could get defensive about it, but even Crepevine is leagues better than this place, and Crepevine is just average.

Avoid it, spend the extra 10 minutes and go somewhere in Oakland or Berkeley.<//text>

< review>
Hot fried Nashville chicken. Need I say more?
Generous chicken tenders or sliders, with french fries, Mac and cheese, and/or kale salad; and drinks, soda or juice.
My only issue is that the strip mall has limited parking.
The tenders are largish, and come wrapped in a slice of bread. Choice of heat goes from balmy to nuclear, which I was too chicken to try.
Sliders (tenders) come in a bun with Mac and cheese. Inside the bun.</review>

This is the closest sporting goods store to fisherman's wharf. They are open late for anyone needing tackle or gear before leaving out on an offshore trip. They had everything I needed. The prices are more affordable than the tackle shops at the wharf. My 3 star rating reflects my feelings about the cost of merchandise, the selection, and the fact that it's a larger company (not making any effort to distinguish themselves). Hopefully this is helpful for anyone that goes fishing out of San Diego.< /Text>
